- King is forced to c3 or e1, leaving White's position very uncomfortable

This check disrupts White's coordination and keeps maximum pressure on the position.

make_move f1d1

Player_Black (to Proxy):

Looking at this position, I need to evaluate the key features:

1. I have a very advanced black pawn on d3 — this is extremely powerful
2. White's Queen on a5 is threatening multiple things
3. White has a Rook on a2 and pawns on c2, b2 nearby

**Candidate moves analysis:**

- **d3c2** — The pawn captures the white pawn on c2, and now threatens **two** promotion paths: `c2-c1=Q` (capturing the bishop on c1) AND `c2xb1=Q` (capturing the knight on b1). White is forced to respond with `Ra2xc2` to stop immediate promotion — but this costs White the c2 pawn!

- **d3d2** — Just advances, but White can simply play `Ra2xd2` or even `Rg1-d1` to block promotion without losing material.

**d3c2** is clearly superior: it captures a pawn AND creates a double promotion threat that forces White's rook to waste time recapturing, while also eliminating White's c-pawn structure.

make_move d3c2
